第十九回　春述淫邪奸謀藏木桶　逞智慧妙語騙金箍 GPT4

　　話說魏聘才自得仲雨傳授，依法行之，先於林珊枝面前獻盡慇懃，又於八齡班賠盡辛苦。珊枝本係聯錦部有名小旦，繼進登春班，華公子看中了他，遂以重價買進。後來之八齡班皆係珊枝所教。這林珊枝不消說是音律精通了。魏聘才本是個伶俐人，崑曲唱得絕好，就是吹彈也應酬的上來。更兼舊年一路同著班子來，船中又聽會了許多戲文，到京後又三天兩天的聽戲，自然又添了好些曲子。

　　一日，林珊枝教玉齡唱曲，適值聘才閒闖進來，珊枝就請他坐了，一面教著。剛剛這曲子是聘才最得意的，便在旁幫起腔來，五音不亂，唇齒分明，竟唱得出神入妙，把個林珊枝倒驚倒了。即由此相好，就在華公子面前，朝朝暮暮，稱贊聘才。

　　華公子是最信珊枝的，他又不輕易贊人，他肯贊好，必是真好了，心上就有了這個人。那八齡班內的都是些蘇、揚人，脾氣自然相合。聘才會討好，今日送這個一把扇子，明日送那個一個荷囊，總是稱心稱意，小孩子喜歡的東西，覺得這位師爺實在知趣。至於管總的、辦事的，尤巴結得周到，不到一月，竟人人說起好來。閻、王二公是不必說，就張、顧兩位雖然也會拉攏，無如總不及聘才之和氣周匝，鞠躬盡瘁的光景。

　　一日，打聽華公子出門去了，聘才約了張笑梅出城。笑梅要找馮子佩，二人同車即到馮子佩家來。這子佩是與華公子最熟的，已與聘才見過，彼此合式。馮子佩也是個宦家子弟，只因早喪嚴親，又積些宦囊，其母鍾愛，任憑他遊蕩歌場，結交豪貴，後來家業漸漸蕭條。又虧了幾個好友幫扶，所以覺得銀錢應手，服御鮮華，其一種嬌憨柔媚的情況，卻令人可憐可愛。

　　這天張、魏兩人出來，帶著一個小使，到了子佩門口，著小使進去問了。剛好在家，請了進去，到書房坐下。聘才是初次登堂，看那屋子是朝北兩間，鋪設倒也華麗，就覺得滿桌子東西，殘書、筆、硯、玩器等物顛顛倒倒亂雜無章。壁間掛些簫管、琵琶，又有刀箭等物。聘才對笑梅說道：「小馮這麼一個樣兒，怎麼屋子裡東西，也不檢點檢點。」笑梅笑道：「他未必有檢點的工夫，世間人最沒有他忙的。」說著子佩走將出來，此時四月盡天氣，一身羅綺，愈顯得嫋娜多姿。未出屏門，先就是一個笑聲出來，嚷道：「你們來做什麼，可是來給二太爺請安的嗎？」聘才笑著要說話，張笑梅上前，便一把摟得緊緊的，子佩也就摟了笑梅，大家抱了一抱腰。笑梅笑嘻嘻的道：

　　「正是來給二太爺請安的。」便把子佩臉上聞了一聞，又道：「好香！到不是二太爺，直是個小哥兒。」子佩道：「你又浪，鬧得二太爺心上受不得。」聘才在旁大笑，三人廝混一陣，然後坐了，卻大家講不出什麼話來。」

　　聽得門口有人嚷道：「馮老二在家嗎？」子佩接著道：「沒有在家。」聘才聽得聲音很熟，只見一個直闖進來，道：「好阿！你在洞裡頭，還答應不在家。」眾人一看，原來是楊梅窗，皆是熟識的，更為熱鬧了，大家說些無非是遊戲歡樂的話。四人商議道：「難道今日說些閒話，就算了事不成，可不辜負了韶光麼？」笑梅道：「我們是打算聽戲的。」馮子佩道：「呸！鄉里人進城不認得明角燈，當是豬溺泡。今日是忌辰，還想聽戲呢。」楊梅窗道：「今日果然是忌辰，咱們做什麼，上館子去罷。」三人都也高興，子佩又進去換了衣裳，即同步行出門，到了一個酒樓。

　　走堂的見是四個少年，且認得楊、馮二人，便覺高興，知道今日熱鬧的。楊八爺道：「吃什麼？」馮子佩對著走堂的道：「你報上來。」走堂的一一報了數十樣，四人就點了五六樣，先吃起來再說。走堂的先燙上四壺黃酒，一桌果碟兒，遂一樣一樣擺上來。四人飲了一回，又說些笑話，梅窗道：「咱們就這麼算了，叫走堂的也瞧不起，叫個人罷。」聘才是最高興的，便道：「很好，叫誰呢？」梅窗笑道：「我意中人卻多，又喜歡新鮮，不比人家天天總叫那個人。我前日見聯珠班內有個叫玉林，生得很好，一下臺就有人同了出去，想是很紅的。」聘才道：「料沒有琴官好。」梅窗道：「那個琴官？」聘才就把新年看戲的話，略述了些，又道：「這琴官除了梅庾香之外，其餘見了總是冰冷的，恐怕叫他不來。」梅窗道：「那裡有叫不動的相公，今日你就叫他。」聘才心內想道：「如今我在華府，他們也應該知道了，自然看我不比從前，就去叫他，如若不來，再叫別個。」梅窗又問笑梅道：「叫誰？」笑梅道：

　　「我叫蓉官罷。」又問子佩，子佩道：「叫了三人，也就熱鬧。我不叫，我算吃鑲邊酒罷。」梅窗笑道：「你自己算了相公罷。「子佩聽了，含了一口酒，望著梅窗劈面噴來，梅窗一閃，身上卻灑了好些。梅窗道：「何必一句話如此著急，必定說著了你的真病。」大家一笑。就將衫子脫下要些燒酒噴了，放在簷下欄杆上晾了，便又笑道：「可惜這口酒糟蹋了，你何不吐在我口裡？」子佩又抓些瓜子殼撒過來，梅窗也就受之而不報了。

　　只見那走堂的進來道：「琴官、玉林都說病著不能來，蓉官就來。」聘才原料琴官不來的，只好罷了。倒是楊梅窗心上不快，說道：「怎麼叫三個人，倒有兩個不來？不知是真病呢，還是推托的？笑梅道：「自然是真病，推托什麼。」聘才道：「還有個琪官也是很好的，我正月裡叫過他幾回，倒是全來的。」聘才又寫了條子去叫琪官，梅窗另叫了二喜。走堂的道：「琪官打發人去叫了。二喜在那邊陪客已經吃過飯，就散了。」

　　走堂的知會了二喜，不多一刻，二喜就過來，對各人請過安，就在梅窗肩下坐了。斟了一巡酒，送了一巡菜，便問道：「今日席間還叫誰？」梅窗道：「叫的都是有病的，不能來。」聘才見了二喜，便不大歡喜，因正月裡吃了他多少刻薄話。二喜倒不記在心，且那日開發，聘才明日即已送去，沒有漂他的，所以二喜還看得起，遂問聘才道：「從前那一位姓什麼？那個瞅瞅眼兒。叫小利偷了銀了的，如今總不見他。」聘才道：「我如今在城裡住了，這些朋友是不大往來的了。」二喜道：「你在城裡什麼地方？」聘才道：「華公府。」二喜道：「哎呀！華公府。」又問張笑梅住處，笑梅道：「我同他在一個宅子裡。」二喜道：「聽得華公府裡，天天唱戲，他府裡有班子？」聘才道：「有幾班呢。」二喜就到各人面前勸酒，猜拳吃皮杯的，無所不至。

　　鬧了一陣，只不見蓉官、琪官到來。笑梅道：「奇了，今日是忌辰，倒叫不出相公來。」二喜道：「還有那個？」笑梅道：「你們班裡的琪官，還有聯珠的蓉官。」二喜道：「蓉官，我出門時見他到三合樓去的，只怕還沒有散。」梅窗道：「那玉林是你們同班的，他真有病嗎？」二喜道：「玉林阿！不要說起，他同琪官前日都鬧了一件事，幾乎鬧出人命來。他們的師傅，此刻還不依，要去告那個人。琪官今日也不能來的。」於是大家問起什麼事，二喜道：「說來話長，且喝兩鍾再說。」眾人又乾了幾杯。聘才聽說琪官鬧事，便又問二喜道：「你就說來，大家聽聽。」二喜道：「有一位廣東奚十一老爺，你們相好不相好？」三人說都不相識，馮子佩道：「我會過這人，卻不相好，你有話盡說。」二喜道：「這奚老爺是在京候選的，聽說帶了幾萬銀子進來，要捐一個大官。誰知用動了，就湊不上了，只捐了一個知州。這個人真算個闊手，他一進京先認識登春班春蘭，就天天把春蘭放在屋裡，衣裳、金鐲子、熱車等類，就不用講了。春蘭的戲最多的，他於春蘭每一齣戲，做十幾副行頭，首飾都是金的，只怕就要值萬把銀子。春蘭的師傅，故意把春蘭叫回，嘔他賺他，零零碎碎，又花得不少。後來替春蘭出師，又花了五千弔，春蘭就跟了他，天天一炕吹煙，一桌吃飯。譬如這一樣菜，春蘭嚐一嚐說咸了，或是淡了，他就連碗砸了。幾百吊錢做件皮褂子，春蘭說：『風毛出得不好，我不要。』他瞧一瞧真不好，順手一撕，撕做幾塊，再做好的。這算自己的冤脾氣也罷了。既同春蘭這麼相好，就不該鬧別人了，他卻不管，只要他中意，不管人肯不肯，一味的硬來。」眾人都靜悄悄的聽他講，聘才道：「問你玉林、琪官的事，你倒盡拿這冤桶講不完了。」二喜笑道：「一路講下來，橫豎比戲還好聽些。他哄人有多少法子呢！他是嘉應州人，所以有那西洋好法兒。他引誘人先是以銀錢買動人家的心，也有那不愛銀錢倒愛人品呢。這奚老爺相貌生得粗鹵，又高又大，是個武官樣兒，說話也蠢。又吹煙，一天要一兩，臉上是青黑的。」梅窗道：「快說，什麼西洋好法兒？」二喜道：「他有個木桶，口小底大，洋漆描金的。裡頭丁丁當當的響，倒像鐘的聲音。

　　上頭有個蓋子，中間一層板，板底下有個橫檔兒，外頭一個銅鎖門，瞧是瞧不見什麼。他看上了那人，要是不順手的，便哄他到內室去瞧桶兒。人家聽見裡頭響，自然爬在那桶邊上瞧了，奚十一就拿些東西，或是金銀錁子，或是翡翠頑意等類，都是貴重的東西，望桶裡一扔，說你能撿出來，就是你的。那人如何知道細底，便伸手下去。原來中間那層板子有兩個孔兒，一個只放得一隻手，摸不著，又伸下那隻手，他就拿鑰匙往鎖門裡一撥，這兩隻手再退不出來，桶又提不起來，鞠著身子。他就不問你願不願，就硬弄起來。要他興盡了才放你，你叫喊也不中用，已經如此了。即放開了，也無可如何。知機的就問他多要些東西，還有那不知機的與他鬧，他就翻了，倒說訛他，打了罵了。還要送到坊裡收拾你。坊官們大半是他們一路的，送了去拘禁起來，百般的挫辱，還要師傅拿錢去贖，極少也要百十弔。這是奚十一的行為。你說玉林與琪官怎樣鬧事呢？就是這奚十一，頭一次在玉林家吃酒。玉林是忠厚人，不會奉承的。他卻看上了玉林，就是一套衣裳，一對鐲子，又賞他師傅四十弔，因此動了火。第二回單請他，叫玉林陪他，並不多請人，他又賞一百弔。玉林是嫌他那個樣子，總和他生生兒的，他心上就惱了。第三回他師傅又請了許多相公，再請他，他便不來了。他師傅總想他是個大頭，逼著玉林去請安。他更壞，大約心裡就打定主意，留玉林吃飯，又灌了玉林幾杯酒，也騙他看那桶子。不曉得玉林在那裡風聞這個桶是哄人的，就不去看。他沒法了，只好強姦起來。仗著力氣大，就按住了玉林，玉林不依，大哭大喊的。他的跟班聽見了，要進來瞧。奚家的人又不准他進來，他就硬闖了進來。只見按住了玉林，已經扯脫褲子了，看見有人進來才放手，只得說與他頑笑，小孩子不知趣。玉林就一路整著衣裳，哭罵出來，跟班的又在門房嚷了幾句，他要打玉林，沒有趕得上，所以氣極送了坊了，這也可以算了。真真活該有事，這是早上。到將晚的時候，他又叫了琪官。這琪官的性子，你們也知道的，如何肯依呢？他就哄他去瞧桶兒，琪官不知，卻上了當了，兩隻手都放進去，縮不出來，他也要如法炮製，來扯琪官小衣裳。琪官明白了，就是一腿，剛剛踢著那話兒，便疼得要死，就蹲了下去。」說到此，張、魏二人就大樂起來，說：「該！該！這樣東西必有天報。酒又換了，我們共賀一杯。」馮子佩也不言語，楊梅窗道：

　　「你快說罷。」二喜也喝了酒，又說道：「這琪官也苦極了，手又縮不出來，便使起性子來，不顧疼痛，用力亂扭，把那機巧扭壞了，琪官這兩隻手卻刮得稀爛，血淋淋的，也就哭罵出來。他因小腦袋疼痛，也就躲了。琪官回去告訴了師傅，他與袁寶珠相好，又告訴了寶珠，寶珠氣極，便進怡園與徐老爺說了。徐老爺就大怒道：『天下有這種東西，就容他這公樣，這還了得！』又曉得了玉林之事，即著人去向坊裡，連夜把玉林要了出來。一面打算告訴巡城都老爺，要搜他那個桶子，辦他。徐老爺是個正直人，說話是不知避人的，不知有人怎樣通了風。奚十一也怕鬧事，又因銀子用完了，西帳也不拉了，趕著在吏部花了錢，告了個資斧不繼，出京去了。聞說到天津去了，只怕躲幾天就要來的，所以玉林氣壞了，琪官也病了，手還沒有好，怎麼得出來？說完了，你們吃一大杯罷，我舌頭也乾了。」

　　說得眾人個個大笑稱奇。馮子佩道：「這個狗雞巴蛋的，實在可恨，他不管什麼人，當著年輕貌美的，總可以頑得的，他也不瞧自己的樣兒。」梅窗笑道：「你這麼恨了，莫非看過他的寶貝桶子麼？」子佩把梅窗啐了兩口。梅窗道：「他這個桶子，咱們京裡不知會做不會做？」笑梅笑道：「你也要學樣子麼？」梅窗笑了一笑。聘才笑對二喜道：「你講得這麼清楚，這桶子你想必看過的了。」二喜臉上一紅，便斜睃了一眼，就要擰聘才的嘴。梅窗道：「他未必要用著桶子。」二喜又將梅窗擰了兩把，說道：「咱們作買賣的人，有錢就好，何必那樣拿身分呢。可惜他們不像你能會看風水，所以才吃了這場苦。」

　　說罷自己也笑了。聘才心中暗忖道：「倒不料琴官、琪官，既唱了戲，還這麼傲性子，有骨氣，這也奇了。」即問二喜道這奚十一到底是什麼人？這樣橫行霸道，又這樣有錢？」二喜道：「我聽得春蘭講，說也是個少爺，他家祖太爺做過布政司，他父親現做提督呢。」聘才道：「如今春蘭呢？」二喜道：「同出去了。」於是大家又談談笑笑，又喝了一回酒。看看天氣將晚，笑梅、聘才皆要進城，只得算了賬。梅窗又與二喜說定，明日開發。梅窗讓聘才等一同進城，他卻住在城外，又到子佩處，兩個同吃了一回煙，拉了子佩，到胭脂巷玉天仙家去了。

　　再說潘其觀自從被蕙芳哄騙之後，心中著實懊惱，意欲收拾蕙芳，又怕他的交遊闊大，幫他的人多。二者淫心未斷，尚欲再圖實在。又心疼這二百吊錢，倒有些疑心張仲雨與蕙芳串通作弄他，就對仲雨嘮嘮叨叨，說些影射的話。仲雨受了這冤枉，真是無處可伸，便恨起潘三來。他既疑我，我索性坑他一坑，打算要串通蕙芳來算計他。潘三又因保定府城有幾間布鋪，親去查點一番，耽擱了兩月回來。清閒無事，與老婆鬧了幾場，受了些悶氣，無人可解。又想要到蕙芳處作樂，也不同張仲雨，一人獨來。

　　是日已是傍晚，可可走到蕙芳門口，恰就遇著蕙芳從春航處回來。蕙芳一見是潘三，心上著實吃了一驚，只得跳下車來，讓潘三爺進內。潘三便攙著蕙芳的手，喘吁吁走進裡面，到客房坐下。蕙芳便問道：「潘三爺，這幾天總不見你，在那裡發財？你能總不肯賞駕。記得那一天是因華公子住在城外，傳了我去，實在短伺候，你不要怪，咱們相好的日子正長呢。」潘三見蕙芳慇懃委宛，便把從前的氣忿消了一半，便慢慢的說道：「我來做什麼，我也知道你嫌我，二百吊錢倒買張老二吐了我一臉酒。兔子藏在窟窿裡，叫野貓饞著嘴空想呢。」蕙芳聽了這話十分有氣，只得裝著笑道：「你能說話真有趣，今日做什麼，咱們找個地方坐坐罷。」潘三道：「還找什麼地方，你這裡很好。但是我發了誓，戒了酒了，我今是一口不喝了。」蕙芳聽了更是著急，想道：今日真不好了，偏是一個人，酒也不喝，走是不肯走的。我托故要走，他未必肯依。左思右想，臉上漸覺紅暈起來，便自己怔了半天，發恨道：「索性留他，我若怕了他，我也不叫蘇蕙芳了。」便道：「三爺你不喝酒，飯是要吃的。」潘三便點點頭，蕙芳便親自到廚房去了一回，便擺出飯來了：三葷三素，一碗紹興湯，又一壺黃酒。

　　蕙芳道：「雖然戒了酒，既到我這裡，也要應個景兒。」便滿臉帶笑，拿了一個大玉杯，斟得滿滿的，雙手送去。那潘三原未戒酒，不過怕酒誤事。今見蕙芳如此，便忍不住笑嘻嘻道：「可盡這一壺，不許再添了。」蕙芳也不理他，於是兩人對飲，又吃些扁食之類。潘三已有醉意，喝來喝去，又添了一壺，見蕙芳桃花兩頰，秋水雙波，顧盼生嬌，媚態百出，把個潘三的故態又引出來了，歎口氣道：「你這個孩子真真害死我，二百吊錢算什麼，你不犯害人！兒子，你只要一點心到我身上，我是沒有不依的。」蕙芳強笑道：「三爺，我不懂得，什麼叫依不依？」潘三道：「只要你有心於我，你要什麼我總依的。」蕙芳笑道：「未必能依罷？我要，要是要一個銀號，這是你自己說過的。」潘三道：「銀號我有三個，我已經四十八歲了，還沒有兒子，給你一個銀號，也沒有什麼要緊。你給我什麼呢？」蕙芳只不言語。潘三道：「怎麼又不說？就是咱父爺兒倆，又沒有外人，有什麼說不得的話嗎？」蕙芳總是似笑非笑的不言語，潘三便坐近來，將蕙芳摟在懷裡，自己把那糖糟似的臉，想貼那粉香玉暖的臉，蕙芳將手隔住，輕輕的道：「你倒太胡纏了，你放了手，我才說。」潘三把臉在他手背上擦了又擦，喘吁吁的道：「好兒子，好乖乖，快講罷。」蕙芳故作怒容道：「三爺，你這般性急，我又不講了。」潘三只得鬆了手，蕙芳手上已流了些吐沫，便將手巾擦了，站起來，正色的說道：「潘三爺，我又不是糊塗蟲，你道我瞧不透你的心事？但我既唱了戲，也就講不得乾淨話兒。但是我今年才十八歲，又出了師，外面求你留我一點臉，當一個人，不要這麼歪纏我，我有心就是了，莫叫人瞧破。你別當我是剃頭篷子的徒弟。三爺你心裡想我使了你二百吊錢，你捨不得，如果要，我也還得出來。」潘三道：「好兒子，那個要你還錢？你怪不得我，我整整兒想了半年了，你不叫我舒服一舒服。你若真有心就好了，你只怕還是賺我。你再要我上當，我就不依了。橫豎你的話我沒有不遵的。」

　　蕙芳又笑道：「我方才說，三爺是逛慣剃頭篷子的，拿我這裡當作一樣。我聽張仲雨說，潘三爺是大方得很的，只要中意那人，不但三百五百，就是一千八百弔都肯。怎麼三爺又瞧得中我，你在我面上才花過二百吊錢，馬上就要撈本兒。要說二百吊錢，不但三爺看不上，就是我姓蘇的也不當事，難道三爺喝一杯酒，聽一個曲兒，還不賞個百十吊錢嗎？也像那些小本經紀人，叫一天相公給個四弔五弔京錢？告訴你：只要你能真有心，我准不負你。你可不要忘了我，當我是個下作人，遂了你的心，你倒拉倒了，又疼別人去了，那時可莫怪我。」潘三被蕙芳一席話，說得無言可答。聽他句句應允，覺要錢多，二百弔尚少的意思。既而又想道：「這等紅相公，自然是不輕容易到手的。」便對蕙芳道：「你真不負我，我就放心了。但是口說無憑，後來恐又變了卦。」蕙芳冷笑道：「你千不放心，萬不放心，難道寫張契約與你嗎？」

　　潘三此時色心豔豔，又要裝作大方，倒不能粗鹵起來，想一想，只好再把銀錢巴結他，便道：「知你是個闊相公，手筆大，常要用錢，打今日起，如少錢，便即到我舖子裡來取。」蕙芳道：「我怎麼好來？不要叫三奶奶曉得了，一頓臭罵，害得你還要受苦呢！」潘三笑道：「胡鬧，你實對我說，到底少錢不少錢？」蕙芳想一想道：「這東西被我刻薄了，他還不懂，還想拿錢來買我，索性賺這糊塗蟲，也好給田郎作膏火之費。便帶笑道：「錢是怎麼不要呢，我不好講，又恐三爺疑心我盡賺錢，一點好處沒有，錢倒花得多呢。」說罷便看著自己手上的翡翠鐲子，便取下來，給潘三瞧道：「你瞧瞧這翡翠好不好？」潘三一看，覺得璧清如水，而且係全綠的，便贊道：「好翠，城裡頭少，只怕是雲南來的。」蕙芳道：「是怡園徐老爺賞的，一樣四個給了四個人，我得了一個。聽說在廣東買來，一個是一塊花邊錢。」潘三吐了吐舌，講道：「比金的還貴，十兩重的也不過二百銀。」蕙芳道：「好雖好，可惜沒個金的配他。」一頭瞧著潘三手腕上有個很重的金箍。潘三心上明白，意欲賞他，恰有十兩重，值二百銀，又覺心疼；若不賞他，又恐被他看不起，便不答應了。

　　自己抬了膀子看了一回，對蕙芳道：「將這個配上就好了，你要就給你罷。」只管抬著膀子，卻不見取下來。蕙芳走近身邊，謝了一聲，將鐲子取下，剛剛帶上了手，卻被潘三攔腰抱住，口口心肝兒子，臉上嗅個不住，便就摳摳摸摸起來。此番蕙芳真沒有法，再講什麼話，潘三是再不理的了。打定主意今日是不肯空回白轉的，況且又把個金鐲子出脫了，臉上已覺得十分光彩。蕙芳只得裝作笑容，見他衣襟上掛著個小牙梳子，便把他的鬍鬚梳了一回。正在危急之際，只聽外面有人嚷道：「蕙芳在家麼？」又聽說：「老父來了！」覺有許多腳步響，蕙芳連忙掙脫道：「不好了！坊官老爺來查夜了。」潘三是個財主，聽見坊官查夜，就著了忙，想要躲避。蕙芳道：「躲是沒有躲處的，就請走罷，省得遇著他們，查三問四起來，倒不好看。」潘三無奈，剛著手時，又衝散了，只得從黑暗處一溜煙跑出大門。不知來的果係何人，且聽下回分解。

Here is the English translation:

After Wei Pingcai learned from Zhong Yu, he followed the instructions meticulously. First, he showed utmost devotion to Lin Shanzhi, and then he endured many hardships with the Eight-year Troupe. Lin Shanzhi, originally a famous young actress from the Lianjin Troupe, later joined the Dengchun Troupe. Master Hua was fond of her and bought her for a high price. Later, Lin Shanzhi taught all the members of the Eight-year Troupe. Lin Shanzhi was known for her mastery of music and drama. Wei Pingcai, being a clever person, sang Kunqu opera excellently and could also play musical instruments well. Having traveled with the troupe the previous year, he learned many plays during the journey and heard more performances in the capital, naturally adding many new pieces to his repertoire.

One day, when Lin Shanzhi was teaching Yuling to sing, Wei Pingcai happened to enter the room. Lin Shanzhi invited him to sit and continued teaching. The song they were practicing was one of Wei Pingcai’s favorites, so he joined in, singing with perfect pitch and clarity, astounding Lin Shanzhi with his extraordinary talent. From that day on, Lin Shanzhi spoke highly of him in front of Master Hua, praising Wei Pingcai every morning and evening.

Master Hua trusted Lin Shanzhi immensely. Since she rarely praised anyone, her approval meant that Wei Pingcai was genuinely outstanding. The members of the Eight-year Troupe, mostly from Suzhou and Yangzhou, naturally got along well with Wei Pingcai. He knew how to win their favor, gifting fans today and sachets tomorrow, always giving things that pleased them. The children especially liked him, considering him very considerate. As for the managers and officials, he flattered them even more skillfully. Within a month, everyone spoke well of him. The two patrons, Yan and Wang, were especially impressed. Even Zhang and Gu, who were also good at currying favor, couldn’t match Wei Pingcai’s amiable and devoted demeanor.

One day, learning that Master Hua had left, Wei Pingcai invited Zhang Xiaomei to go out of the city. Xiaomei wanted to visit Feng Zipei, so they both rode to his house. Feng Zipei was very close to Master Hua and had met Wei Pingcai before, and they got along well. Feng Zipei, the son of an official, had lost his father early and inherited some wealth, allowing his mother to dote on him. This let him indulge in a life of leisure, making friends with influential people, though his family estate gradually declined. Thanks to the help of a few friends, he still had money and dressed lavishly. His charming and gentle demeanor made him both pitiable and lovable.

On this day, Wei Pingcai and Zhang Xiaomei arrived at Feng Zipei’s door with a servant. Feng Zipei was at home and invited them in, taking them to his study. It was Wei Pingcai’s first time there, and he found the two northern rooms luxuriously decorated but cluttered with disorganized books, brushes, inkstones, and other items. Musical instruments like flutes and pipa, as well as swords and arrows, hung on the walls. Wei Pingcai remarked to Xiaomei, “How can someone like Little Feng keep his room so untidy?” Xiaomei laughed and replied, “He probably doesn’t have time to tidy up; he’s the busiest person in the world.” As they spoke, Feng Zipei entered, dressed in fine silk, looking graceful and elegant. Before he even stepped out from behind the screen, his laughter preceded him. He called out, “What are you here for? Are you here to pay respects to your second uncle?” Wei Pingcai was about to speak when Zhang Xiaomei rushed forward, hugging Feng Zipei tightly. Feng Zipei also hugged Xiaomei, and they all shared a laugh. Xiaomei, still smiling, said, “Yes, we are here to pay our respects to our second uncle.” He then sniffed Feng Zipei’s face and said, “How fragrant! You’re not an uncle; you’re a little brother.” Feng Zipei replied, “You’re so playful; your uncle can’t handle it.” Wei Pingcai laughed loudly, and the three of them chatted and laughed for a while before sitting down, though they didn’t have much to say.

They heard someone shouting at the door, “Is Old Feng at home?” Feng Zipei responded, “He’s not here.” Wei Pingcai recognized the voice, and soon someone barged in, saying, “Oh, you’re hiding here and claiming not to be home.” It was Yang Meichuang, a familiar face to everyone, making the gathering even livelier. They talked about various fun and playful topics. The four of them discussed, “Should we just chat today and call it a day? That would be a waste of time, wouldn’t it?” Xiaomei said, “We planned to watch a play.” Feng Zipei responded, “Nonsense! Peasants coming to the city don’t recognize the fancy lanterns, thinking they’re pig troughs. Today is a solemn day, and you still want to watch a play?” Yang Meichuang said, “Today is indeed a solemn day. What should we do? Let’s go to a restaurant.” All three agreed enthusiastically. Feng Zipei went in to change his clothes, and they all walked to a restaurant.

The waiter, recognizing Yang and Feng, was pleased, knowing it would be a lively day. Yang Baoye asked, “What should we eat?” Feng Zipei told the waiter, “You tell us.” The waiter listed dozens of dishes, and the four of them ordered five or six to start. The waiter brought four pots of warm wine and a table of fruit dishes, serving the dishes one by one. After drinking for a while and sharing some jokes, Meichuang said, “Should we end it like this? The waiter will look down on us. Let’s call someone.” Wei Pingcai, the most enthusiastic, said, “Great, who should we call?” Meichuang laughed, “I have many favorites and like variety, unlike others who call the same person every time. Recently, I saw someone named Yulin in the Lianzhu Troupe. He’s very handsome and popular, always accompanied by someone after performances.” Wei Pingcai said, “Not as good as Qin Guan.” Meichuang asked, “Which Qin Guan?” Wei Pingcai then described some scenes from a play he watched, adding, “This Qin Guan, apart from Mei Yuxiang, treats everyone else coldly. I’m afraid he won’t come if we call him.” Meichuang said, “There’s no performer who wouldn’t come when called. Today, you call him.” Wei Pingcai thought, “Now that I’m with the Hua family, they should know and treat me differently than before. I’ll call him, and if he doesn’t come, we’ll call someone else.” Meichuang asked Xiaomei, “Who will you call?” Xiaomei said, “I’ll call Rong Guan.” He then asked Zipei, who replied, “Three people should be enough for a lively time. I won’t call anyone; I’ll just enjoy the show.” Meichuang laughed, “You should consider yourself a performer.” Zipei, hearing this, took a sip of wine and sprayed it at Meichuang, who dodged but still got some on him. Meichuang said, “Why get so worked up over a single remark? It must have hit your sore spot.” Everyone laughed. Meichuang took off his wet shirt, asked for some burning wine to spray on it, and hung it to dry, joking, “What a waste of good wine. Why didn’t you spit it into my mouth?” Zipei threw some melon seed shells at Meichuang, who accepted them without retaliation.

The waiter came in and said, “Qin Guan and Yulin both say they are sick and can’t come, but Rong Guan will come.” Wei Pingcai had expected that Qin Guan wouldn’t come, so he let it go. However, Yang Meichuang was unhappy and said, “Why did we call three people, and two of them can’t come? Are they really sick, or just making excuses?” Xiaomei said, “Of course they are really sick. Why would they make excuses?” Wei Pingcai said, “There’s also Qi Guan, who is very good. I called him a few times during the New Year, and he always came.” Wei Pingcai then wrote a note to call Qi Guan, and Meichuang called for Erxi. The waiter said, “Qi Guan has sent someone to call for him. Erxi is already entertaining guests over there and just finished eating. He will come soon.”

The waiter informed Erxi, and in no time, Erxi came over, greeted everyone, and sat down next to Meichuang. After pouring a round of wine and serving a round of dishes, he asked, “Who else is coming to the banquet today?” Meichuang said, “Those we called are all sick and can’t come.” Seeing Erxi, Wei Pingcai wasn’t very pleased because he had endured many sarcastic remarks from him during the New Year. Erxi, however, didn’t hold any grudges. On that occasion, Wei Pingcai had promptly sent over some gifts the next day, so Erxi still thought well of him. Erxi asked Wei Pingcai, “What was the name of that person before? The one with the squinty eyes, who had his silver stolen by Xiaoli. He hasn’t been seen lately.” Wei Pingcai said, “I now live in the city and don’t socialize with those friends much.” Erxi asked, “Where in the city do you live?” Wei Pingcai said, “At Hua Gong’s mansion.” Erxi exclaimed, “Oh my! Hua Gong’s mansion.” He then asked Zhang Xiaomei where he lived. Xiaomei said, “I live in the same house with him.” Erxi said, “I heard that there’s daily opera singing at Hua Gong’s mansion. Does his household have a troupe?” Wei Pingcai said, “There are several troupes.” Erxi then went around encouraging everyone to drink and play games, making it very lively.

After a while, neither Rong Guan nor Qi Guan had arrived. Xiaomei said, “It’s strange. It’s a solemn day, and we can’t even call any performers.” Erxi asked, “Who else did you call?” Xiaomei said, “Qi Guan from your troupe and Rong Guan from the Lianzhu Troupe.” Erxi said, “Rong Guan, I saw him going to the Sanhe Tower when I left. He probably hasn’t finished yet.” Meichuang asked, “Is Yulin from your troupe really sick?” Erxi said, “Yulin! Don’t mention it. He and Qi Guan got into a fight the other day, almost causing a fatality. Their master is still upset and wants to file a complaint.” Everyone then asked what happened, and Erxi said, “It’s a long story. Let’s have a couple of drinks first.” They all had a few more drinks. Wei Pingcai, hearing that Qi Guan had caused trouble, asked Erxi again, “Tell us the story; we all want to hear it.” Erxi said, “Do you know Mr. Xi Eleven from Guangdong? Are you friends with him?” The three said they didn’t know him. Feng Zipei said, “I’ve met him but we’re not friends. Go ahead and tell us.” Erxi said, “This Mr. Xi is a candidate for an official position in the capital. He supposedly brought several tens of thousands of silver with him, planning to buy a high official position. But he fell short and only managed to buy a prefecture position. This man is quite extravagant. When he first arrived in the capital, he befriended Chunlan from the Dengchun Troupe, keeping her in his house every day, providing her with clothes, gold bracelets, and warm carriages. Chunlan performed many plays, and for each play, Mr. Xi would prepare more than ten sets of costumes, with jewelry all made of gold, costing thousands of silver. Chunlan’s master intentionally called her back to upset him, making him spend even more. Later, when Chunlan graduated, he spent another five thousand strings of cash. Chunlan followed him, and they lived lavishly every day. For example, if Chunlan found a dish too salty or too bland, he would smash the entire bowl. He spent hundreds of strings of cash on a fur coat, and if Chunlan said the fur was not right, he would tear it to pieces and make a new one. This was his temperament. Since he was so close to Chunlan, he shouldn’t have troubled others, but he didn’t care. As long as he liked someone, he would force himself on them regardless of their consent.”

Everyone listened quietly. Wei Pingcai said, “We asked about Yulin and Qi Guan, and you’re telling us this long-winded story.” Erxi laughed, “It’s all connected. His stories are more interesting than a play. He has many tricks to deceive people. Being from Jiayingzhou, he knows many Western tricks. He lures people by offering money, but some people are more interested in his character than his money. Mr. Xi is tall and bulky, with a martial demeanor, and speaks clumsily. He smokes opium, consuming about an ounce a day, making his face dark. Meichuang said, “Get to the point about the Western tricks.” Erxi said, “He has a wooden bucket, narrow at the top and wide at the bottom, painted with gold designs. It makes a ding-dong sound like a bell when shaken. There is a lid on top, and a middle layer with a horizontal bar underneath, with a copper lock on the outside. He uses it to trick people he fancies. If they resist, he lures them into a room to look at the bucket. Hearing the sound inside, people naturally look into it. Mr. Xi then throws in some valuables, saying they can keep whatever they retrieve. Unaware of the trick, they reach in, but the bottom layer has holes only big enough for one hand at a time, making it impossible to retrieve the items. As they reach in with both hands, he locks the door, trapping their hands. Unable to pull out their hands or lift the bucket, they are at his mercy. Only after he’s satisfied does he release them, and they can’t do anything about it. Those who know better demand more compensation, while those who don’t quarrel with him and get beaten or taken to the police station, where they are detained and humiliated, requiring their master to pay a ransom, often at least a hundred strings of cash. This is Mr. Xi’s way.”

Wei Pingcai asked, “What happened between Yulin and Qi Guan?” Erxi continued, “Mr. Xi first attended a banquet at Yulin’s house. Yulin, being honest and straightforward, didn’t flatter him. Mr. Xi took a liking to Yulin, gave him a set of clothes and a pair of bracelets, and rewarded his master with forty strings of cash, igniting his interest. The second time, he invited Yulin alone, rewarding him with a hundred strings of cash. Yulin, disgusted by Mr. Xi’s demeanor, stayed aloof, angering him. The third time, Yulin’s master invited many performers and Mr. Xi again, but he didn’t come. The master, seeing Mr. Xi as a big spender, pressured Yulin to pay respects to him. Mr. Xi got worse, deciding to detain Yulin for a meal, getting him drunk, and tricking him into looking at the bucket. Yulin, having heard of the bucket’s trickery, refused. Mr. Xi, using his strength, pinned Yulin down, who resisted by crying and shouting. Hearing the commotion, his servant tried to enter, but Mr. Xi’s men barred the way. The servant forced his way in and saw Mr. Xi pinning Yulin down with his pants pulled down. Seeing someone enter, Mr. Xi let go, claiming they were just playing around. Yulin left, crying and cursing, and his servant argued with Mr. Xi at the door. Mr. Xi, enraged, sent Yulin to the police station. Later in the evening, he called Qi Guan, who, unlike Yulin, fell for the bucket trick, trapping his hands. Mr. Xi tried to undress Qi Guan, who, realizing the trick, kicked Mr. Xi in the groin, causing him excruciating pain and forcing him to crouch down.”

At this point, Zhang and Wei burst out laughing, saying, “Serves him right! Such a person will get his comeuppance. Let’s toast to this!” Feng Zipei remained silent while Yang Meichuang said:

“Please continue,” urged the others. Erxi took another sip of wine and continued, “Qi Guan was in extreme pain and couldn’t free his hands, so he stubbornly twisted them, breaking the mechanism. His hands were badly scraped and bleeding, and he cried and cursed as he escaped. Because of the pain in his head, he hid away. Qi Guan told his master what happened, and also informed Yuan Baozhu, with whom he was close. Baozhu was furious and went to Yi Garden to speak with Mr. Xu. Mr. Xu was enraged, saying, ‘How can such a person be allowed to act so shamelessly? This is unacceptable!’ Learning about Yulin’s ordeal, he sent people to the station, demanding Yulin’s release overnight. At the same time, he planned to inform the city patrol officer and have that bucket seized, intending to deal with Xi Eleven. Mr. Xu, being a straightforward person, spoke openly about his plans, unaware that someone might have informed Xi Eleven. Fearing trouble and having run out of money, Xi Eleven quickly spent more money at the Ministry of Personnel to claim he was out of funds and left the capital, reportedly heading to Tianjin. He might return after a few days, but Yulin was furious, and Qi Guan was still ill with his hands not yet healed. How could he come out? I’ve finished. You all have a big drink; my tongue is dry.”

Everyone laughed in amazement. Feng Zipei remarked, “This despicable person is truly detestable. He doesn’t care who he is dealing with; as long as they are young and attractive, he assumes he can have his way with them without considering his own appearance.” Meichuang laughed, “You seem to hate him quite a lot. Have you seen his precious bucket?” Zipei spat twice at Meichuang. Meichuang asked, “Could we make such a bucket in our capital?” Xiaomei laughed, “Do you want to follow his example?” Meichuang smiled. Wei Pingcai laughed and said to Erxi, “You describe it so clearly; you must have seen that bucket yourself.” Erxi’s face turned red, and he gave a sidelong glance, ready to pinch Wei Pingcai’s mouth. Meichuang said, “He doesn’t necessarily need to use the bucket.” Erxi pinched Meichuang twice and said, “As businessmen, having money is good. Why put on airs? Unfortunately, they don’t know how to read the situation like you, which is why they suffered.”

He then laughed. Wei Pingcai thought to himself, “I didn’t expect that Qin Guan and Qi Guan, being performers, would be so proud and have such integrity. It’s quite surprising.” He then asked Erxi, “Who exactly is this Xi Eleven? How can he act so outrageously and have so much money?” Erxi replied, “I heard from Chunlan that he is also a young master. His grandfather was a provincial administration commissioner, and his father is currently a military governor.” Wei Pingcai asked, “Where is Chunlan now?” Erxi said, “She left with him.” The group continued talking and laughing and drank some more wine. As the evening approached, Xiaomei and Wei Pingcai needed to return to the city, so they settled the bill. Meichuang arranged with Erxi to settle accounts the next day. Meichuang invited Wei Pingcai and others to return to the city together, but he lived outside the city and went to Zipei’s place, where they smoked for a while. Then they went to Yutianxian’s house in Rouge Alley.

Meanwhile, Pan Qiguan had been quite upset since being tricked by Huifang. He wanted to take revenge on Huifang but feared his influential connections and numerous supporters. Additionally, his lust hadn’t completely subsided, and he still desired another encounter. He regretted losing two hundred strings of cash and suspected Zhang Zhongyu of colluding with Huifang to deceive him. He often grumbled to Zhongyu, making insinuating remarks. Zhongyu, feeling wronged and having no outlet for his frustration, began to resent Pan San. Since Pan San doubted him, Zhongyu decided to collaborate with Huifang to trick Pan San. Pan San, meanwhile, had gone to inspect some cloth shops in Baoding Prefecture, delaying his return by two months. Bored and having quarreled with his wife several times, Pan San felt frustrated and had no one to talk to. He decided to visit Huifang for some entertainment and went alone without Zhang Zhongyu.

That evening, just as he reached Huifang’s door, he coincidentally met Huifang returning from Chunhang’s place. Huifang was startled to see Pan San but got out of the carriage and invited him in. Pan San held Huifang’s hand as they walked inside, breathlessly, and sat in the guest room. Huifang asked, “Master Pan, I haven’t seen you in a while. Where have you been making money? You never visit. Remember, that day, Master Hua was staying outside the city, and he called for me. I couldn’t attend to you properly. Don’t be angry; we have plenty of time ahead.” Pan San, seeing Huifang’s earnestness, felt half of his anger dissipate and slowly said, “I know why I’m here. You despise me, and I wasted two hundred strings of cash just to have Zhang Lao Er spray wine in my face. A rabbit hiding in a hole, making a wildcat drool.” Huifang, hearing this, felt both angry and amused but kept smiling and said, “You have such a way with words. What do you want to do today? Let’s find a place to sit.” Pan San said, “Why go elsewhere? This place is fine. But I’ve sworn off drinking; I won’t have a drop today.” Huifang became anxious, thinking, “This is bad. He’s alone, won’t drink, and won’t leave. If I make an excuse to leave, he won’t agree. Thinking hard, her face flushed, and she decided, ‘I’ll just keep him here. If I’m scared of him, I won’t be Su Huifang.’ She said, “Master Pan, if you won’t drink, you still have to eat.” Pan San nodded, and Huifang personally went to the kitchen and brought out a meal: three meat dishes, three vegetable dishes, a bowl of Shaoxing soup, and a pot of yellow wine.

Huifang said, “Though you’ve sworn off drinking, since you’re here, you should have a drink.” She smiled, took a large jade cup, filled it to the brim, and handed it to him with both hands. Pan San, having not really given up drinking but afraid it might cause trouble, couldn’t resist and said with a smile, “I’ll finish this pot, but no refills.” Huifang ignored him, and they both drank and ate some dumplings. Pan San, now tipsy, saw Huifang’s flushed cheeks, her charming eyes, and her every movement filled with allure, and he couldn’t help but revert to his old ways. Sighing, he said, “You really drive me crazy. What’s two hundred strings of cash? You don’t need to harm people! If you have a heart for me, I won’t refuse you.” Huifang forced a smile and said, “Master Pan, I don’t understand. What do you mean by ‘refuse’?” Pan San said, “If you care for me, I’ll give you anything you want.” Huifang laughed, “Can you really? I want a bank; you said you had one.” Pan San said, “I have three banks. I’m already forty-eight years old and still have no children. Giving you one bank is no big deal. What will you give me in return?” Huifang remained silent. Pan San said, “Why don’t you speak? It’s just us, no outsiders. Why hesitate?” Huifang, still smiling, said nothing. Pan San moved closer, trying to embrace Huifang, pressing his wine-scented face against her fragrant one. Huifang gently pushed him away and said, “You’re too much. Let go, and I’ll speak.” Pan San rubbed his face on her hand, panting, “Good girl, sweetie, tell me quickly.” Huifang pretended to be angry and said, “Master Pan, you’re too impatient. I won’t speak if you keep this up.” Pan San had to let go. Huifang wiped her hand, now wet with his saliva, with a towel, stood up, and sternly said, “Master Pan, I’m not a fool. Do you think I don’t see through you? But since I perform, I can’t speak of purity. However, I’m only eighteen and just graduated. Outside, please respect me and treat me like a person. Don’t pester me like this. If I have a heart for you, don’t let people see through it. Don’t think of me as just an apprentice. If you’re upset about the two hundred strings of cash, I can return it.” Pan San said, “Sweetie, who asked you to return the money? You can’t blame me; I’ve been thinking about you for six months. You won’t let me enjoy myself. If you truly care for me, that’s fine. But if you trick me again, I won’t accept it. I’ll follow your words.”

Huifang laughed again and said, “I just said, Master Pan, you’re used to frequenting brothels and think of my place as the same. I heard from Zhang Zhongyu that Master Pan is very generous; if he takes a liking to someone, he wouldn’t mind spending even a thousand or eighteen hundred taels. But now that you’ve taken a liking to me, you’ve only spent two hundred taels and immediately want to get your money’s worth. Just two hundred taels—Master Pan wouldn’t consider it much, nor would I, Su. Wouldn’t Master Pan at least reward a hundred taels for a drink and a song? You treat me like a small-time broker, paying a performer four or five taels a day. I’ll tell you this: if you truly have feelings for me, I won’t let you down. But don’t think of me as a lowly person to satisfy your desires and then leave me for someone else. If that happens, don’t blame me.”

Pan San was left speechless by Huifang’s words. Hearing her agreeing to everything but hinting that two hundred taels was too little, he thought, “Such a popular performer must be hard to win over.” He said to Huifang, “If you truly won’t let me down, I’ll be at ease. But words are unreliable; you might change your mind later.” Huifang coldly replied, “You don’t trust me at all. Do you want a written contract?”

At this point, Pan San, driven by desire, wanted to appear generous and couldn’t act roughly. After some thought, he decided to win her over with money. He said, “I know you’re a high-status performer who often needs money. From today on, if you need money, come to my shop and take what you need.” Huifang said, “How could I do that? What if Madam Pan finds out and scolds you, causing you trouble?” Pan San laughed, “Nonsense, tell me honestly, do you need money or not?” Huifang thought, “This fool doesn’t understand my hint. He still wants to buy me with money. Fine, I’ll make this fool pay and use it to support Tian Lang.” Smiling, she said, “How could I not need money? I’m reluctant to ask, fearing you might think I’m just after money and not giving anything in return.” She then looked at the jade bracelet on her hand, took it off, and showed it to Pan San, “Look at this jade bracelet; isn’t it beautiful?” Pan San saw that it was clear and green like water, and praised, “Good jade, rare in the city, probably from Yunnan.” Huifang said, “It was a gift from Mr. Xu from Yi Garden. He gave four, one to each of us. I heard he bought it in Guangdong for a fortune.” Pan San stuck out his tongue and said, “It’s more expensive than gold; ten taels of gold aren’t worth two hundred silver.” Huifang said, “Though it’s beautiful, it’s a pity it doesn’t have a gold counterpart.” She glanced at the heavy gold bracelet on Pan San’s wrist. Pan San understood, wanting to gift it to her, but hesitated as it was worth two hundred silver and felt reluctant. Yet, if he didn’t give it, he feared she’d look down on him, so he didn’t respond.

He raised his arm and looked at it for a moment, then said to Huifang, “This would pair well with it. Do you want it? I’ll give it to you.” He kept raising his arm without taking it off. Huifang approached, thanked him, took off the gold bracelet, and put it on her hand. Pan San then hugged her, calling her his sweetheart, smelling her face, and groping her. Huifang, unable to do anything, realized that Pan San was determined not to leave empty-handed today, especially after giving away the gold bracelet. Trying to keep a smile, she saw a small ivory comb on his jacket and combed his beard. Just then, someone shouted outside, “Is Huifang home?” Then they heard, “The police are here!” There were many footsteps. Huifang quickly broke free and said, “It’s bad! The patrol officers are here for a night inspection.” Pan San, being a wealthy man, panicked at the thought of the patrol officers and wanted to hide. Huifang said, “There’s nowhere to hide. You better leave to avoid being questioned.” Pan San had no choice but to leave quickly in the dark, running out the door. Who the visitors were, we will find out next time.

第二十回　奪錦標龍舟競渡　悶酒令鴛侶傳觴 GPT4o

　　前回書中，講到潘三纏住蕙芳，到至急處忽有人嚷進來，蕙芳故作一驚說：「了不得了！是坊官老爺們查夜。」潘三是個有錢膽小的人，自然怕事，只得溜了。

　　原來蕙芳於下廚房時，即算定潘三今日必不甘休，即叫家裡人假裝坊官查夜，並請了兩個坊卒，到潘三歪纏不清的時候，便嚷將進來。知道潘三是色大膽小，果然中計而去，又哄過了一次。雖然得了他一個金鐲，蕙芳心中也著實躊躇，恐怕明日又來，只好到春航寓內躲避幾天，再看罷了。潘三一路喪氣而回，幸怕他的老婆，不敢公然在外胡鬧，不然只怕蕙芳雖然伶俐，也就難招架了。今天又空鬧了一場，只好慢慢兒再將銀錢巴結他，買轉他的心來。

　　這回書又要說幾個風雅人，做件風雅事情。如今這一班名士，漸漸的散了。子玉自從與琴言怡園一敘之後，總未能會面。

　　琴言之病，時好時發，也不進園子唱戲，有時力疾到怡園一走。

　　而子玉之病亦係憂悶而起，或到怡園時，偏值琴言不來；或到琴言寓裡，偏又逢著他們有事，不是他師傅請客，就是有人坐著。又不便再尋素蘭，子玉亦覺得無可奈何，只好悵恨緣慳而已。這邊琴言在家，並不知子玉來過幾次，又聽得子玉害病，心上更是悲酸，因為沒有到過梅宅，不便自去。正是一點憐才慕色之心，無可寬解，惟有短歎長吁，形諸夢寐。看官，你道子玉去尋琴言，為什麼他的師傅總不拉攏呢？一來子玉是逢場作戲，不是常在外面的人，是以長慶不相認識，且不曉得子玉是何等地位，不過當他一個年輕讀書人，無甚相與處。二來子玉在琴言身上，也沒有花過一個錢。子玉與琴言是神交心契，自然想不到這些上來。那長慶則惟在錢多，卻不在人好。那下作相公們的脾氣，總是這樣，那長慶生性如此，是始終不變的。

　　且說子玉是在家養病，不出大門，高品為河間胡太尊請去修志，劉文澤是他岳母惦記他，來接他並其室吳氏，同到直隸總督衙門去了。此中已少了三人，只有子雲、次賢、南湘、仲清、春航、王恂六人，不時往來。

　　一日，子雲、次賢招諸名士到園看龍舟，並賞榴花。此日是五月初一，正值王通政生日，雖不做壽，家中卻也有些至交好友親戚同年來賀，內裡又有些太太姑娘們，如梅宅的顏夫人，孫宅的陸夫人之類，也覺得熱鬧。王恂與仲清這怡園之約，就不能去了。是日子雲、次賢知道了，也去拜拜壽，適遇南湘、春航皆在，就約了回來。仲清、王恂說如客散得早，也來赴約。

　　但只不要候，遲早不定。次賢等應了，才回怡園，同到了迎面峭壁之下。進了一個院落，子雲便請大家寬了公服。又道：「今日天氣甚熱，紅日照人，且龍舟在吟秋水榭，榴花在小赤城，離此頗遠，不如乘馬過去。」家人們已預先備馬伺候，即帶過來，四人都乘上了。從峭壁下左手轉彎，高高低低，曲曲折折，走上青石羊腸小徑，有些古藤礙首，香草鉤衣。走完了山徑，便順著圍牆而走，那邊是池水漣漪，依紅泛綠，堤上一帶短短紅闌，修竹垂楊，還有些雜花滿樹，流鶯亂飛，已令人塵襟盡浣。不到半里，又是一堆危石，疊成高山，有十丈多高，如羅浮一峰，俯瞰海曲，擋住去路。

　　子雲請客下了馬，從山腳走上石級，三十餘層，有一小亭，中具石臺石凳，署名曰「縹緲亭」。對面望去，有幾十株蒼松，黛色參天的遮斷眼界，樹杪處微露碧瓦數鱗，朱樓一角。此間頗覺清風蕩漾，水石清寒，飄飄乎有凌虛之想。春航道：「奇奧！文心一至於此，即匡廬之香爐峰，何以過之。」南湘道：「前似王麓臺，此似蕭尺木，幽邃處卻不險仄。」子雲道：「此皆靜宜手筆，佈置時曾數易其稿。」次賢道：「也虧那幾株松樹，不然也就一望易盡。」春航道：「正不知靜宜先生胸中有多少丘壑，的是驅排河嶽神手。倪雲林、徐青藤定當把臂入林。」次賢只得謙讓幾句。四人小憩了一回，走下石磴來，側面有五間樓閣，恰作參差高下兩層，似樓非樓，似閣非閣，畫棟飛雲，珠簾捲雨，又是一番氣象。窗前闌干外，就是一個十畝方塘，內有層疊荷錢，一半成蓋。中間一座六曲紅橋，欹欹斜斜，接著對面十數間樓榭。右邊泊著幾只小小的畫船，都是錦纜牙牆，蘭橈桂槳。次賢道：「那邊就是吟秋水榭了。」再望水榭，卻是三層，左手一帶是一色楊柳低拂水面，接著對岸修竹長林，竟似兩岸欲合。

　　當下子雲讓客且慢過橋，先進那閣裡來，恰是正正三間，細銅絲穿成的簾子，水磨楠木雕闌，閣中擺設，精緻異常，說不盡寶鼎瑤琴，璇幾玉案。闌邊放一個古銅壺，插著幾枝竹箭，中懸一額，曰：「停雲敘雨之齋。」旁有一聯，其句云：拜石有時具袍笏。看雲無處不神仙。署款為華光宿。南湘失驚道：「此華公子手筆，不料其詞翰如此。」子雲道：「華公子天分極高，不過工夫稍淺，亦其勢位所誤。若論書、畫、詩、詞，倒與其境遇相反的。」春航道：「若僅聞於流俗之口，幾乎失是人矣。即此聯句，可見其胸次之雅；即此書法，可見其意氣之豪。」說罷，遠遠望見水榭邊，蕩出兩個花艇來，白舫青簾尚隔著紅橋綠柳，咿啞柔櫓之聲，宛轉彩蓮之曲，正是水光如鏡，樓臺倒影，飛燕低掠，游魚仰吹，須臾之間已過紅橋，慢慢攏橋，慢慢攏過來。只見王蘭保掖起羅衫，盤了辮髮，鬢邊倒插一枝榴花，手中拿一根小小的紫竹篙，一面撐，一面趕那些家鳧野鴨，倒驚得鴛鴦、溪鳥亂飛起來。又有一個白鷺鷥，竟迎著闌干翩然而來，到了簷前，把翅一側，已飛上山岩去了。

　　次賢笑道：「所謂『打鴨驚鴛鴦』，今日見了。」大家正看得有趣，又見船中走出幾枝花來。一隻船內是寶珠、漱芳，一隻船內是蕙芳、素蘭，共是五個。舟人把舟泊近闌干，南湘道：「芙蓉未開，水榭減色。有此眾芳一渡，庶不寂寞。湘娥洛神，江湄遊戲，我度香先生當以玉佩要之。」大家笑了一笑，群旦上來都見過了。次賢道：「你們看靜芳窄袖踟躕的，越顯得風流跌宕。竹君之贊語『翩若驚鴻，婉若游龍』，真覺得摹擬入神。」南湘道：「靜芳之倜儻，媚香之靈慧，瑤卿之柔婉，瘦香之妍靜，香畹之丰韻，皆是天仙化人。若以其藝而觀，則趙飛燕之掌上舞，張靜婉之帳中歌，可以彷彿。」子雲請客登舟，南湘等上得船來。看那船頭，是刻著兩個交頸鴛鴦，船身是棠梨木的，兩邊短短紅闌，內是玻璃長窗，篷蓋上罩著個綠泥灑花大卷篷，兩邊垂下白綾畫花走水。船裡是兩個艙，底下鋪了細白絨毯，靠後也是長窗，中間鋪設一炕，兩旁是鬼子穿藤小椅，間著幾張茶几，中間一張圓桌，也可以坐得五六人。那一個船略小了些，是坐那侍從人的。此時王蘭保卻早換好了衣裳，斯斯文文的坐了。寶珠對南湘道：「你們早上到過王大人家沒有？」南湘尚未回言，子雲道：「我就在王宅邀來的。」

　　於是眾人談談講講，一路看園中的景致，有幾處是飛閣凌霄，雕甍瞰地。有幾處是危崖突兀，老樹槎木牙。卻也望見西北上一帶長廊是桃塢，接著是杏村；正北上竹林中望去是梨院，後是牡丹香國；東北是一帶玲瓏巧山，下是綠陰千樹，金彈離離，結滿了梅子，青黃各半，把個梅崦遮住，看不清楚。對岸樹石蒙茸，卻不知還有多少亭院。春航問南湘道：「這園子裡共遊過幾處了？」南湘道：「到卻到過許多回，逛卻沒有逛到。一喝酒就是一天，那裡能逛。約有七八處逛過。」寶珠道：「我同瘦香是逛完的了。」蕙芳道：「我就是桂嶺、菊畦、蘭徑沒有到過，其餘也都逛完。」

　　素蘭道：「桂嶺在前山前，蘭徑、菊畦是在後山後，過澗去一片大空地，有一所莊院，便是菊畦。那蘭徑是山下，到半山，高高下下的長廓曲徑，最好頑的所在。菊畦過去還有個稻莊。有桔槔戽水，像個村落，漁簾蟹籪，各樣都有。還有兩個鶴欄、鹿棚，也近在那裡。」

　　說罷船已行了半里多，已到轉彎處，池水卻也空闊。吟秋水榭造在水中，四面周圍有池水圍住，共是三層；只見第一層是十二間，作個六面樣式，面面開窗，純用玻璃鑲嵌的雕窗，隔作六處。一處之中又分陰陽明暗，仍是十二處，大小方圓扁側，又不一樣，各成形勢。內中的擺設，是說不盡的。在這間，看那間只隔一層玻璃，到過去時，卻要轉了好幾處，方能過去。當下諸人，就在這第一層逛了好一回時候。子雲道：「客也餓了，此刻將近午正，可以坐罷。」只見四個小童托上四個金漆盤來，放著幾碗杏酪，分送各人面前，各人吃了。春航道：「索性上那兩層再回來坐罷。」於是轉上樓梯，上了第二層，略小了些，是四面樣式，空出一轉回廓，有闌干迴護，也有雕窗隔作八處，古玩器皿一樣的精雅。望見東北角上柳陰中，泊著龍舟，有三丈多高，舟身子是刻成彩畫一條青龍，中間卻是五六層架子裝起，純用五彩綢緞綾錦氈泥，製成傘蓋旗幡，繡的灑線平金打子各種花卉，還搭配些孔雀泥金傘、珍珠傘、銀針穿成的傘，中間又裝上些剪彩樓臺庭院，王宮梵宇，裝點古蹟。內中人物都是走線行動，機巧異常。一層一層的裝湊起來，為錦為雲，如荼如火。頂上站著一個紮成的金毛孔雀，船內用石壓底，兩邊共有二十四人蕩槳。有個八音班，在內打動鑼鼓絲竹，粗細十番。此是次賢在江蘇看過，畫出圖樣，選匠造製。春航是從南邊來，也曾見過，即道：「實在製得華麗，就是常州府的龍舟，是甲於一省的，也不過如此。」

　　大家又上了第三層，卻是三面式樣，外面也是三面回廓，中間隔作六處。此中窗櫥門戶，是一色香楠木，十分古拙，更為雅靜。地位既高，得氣愈爽，憑闌一望，怡園的全景已收得八九分，只有山陰處尚不能見。惟覺樓臺層疊，花木扶疏，芳草如碧毯平鋪，清泉如水銀直瀉，水如縈帶，山列主賓，多處不見其繁，少處不嫌其略。天然圖畫，輞川圖不過如斯。人力經營，平泉莊何足道也。眾人各自憑闌，遙望四處，只聽龍舟內簫鼓悠揚，清波蕩漾的划將出來。

　　龍尾上掛著個鞦韆架子，兩個孩子一上一下的打鞦韆。次賢道：「還請到底下去看罷，自上望下，不如自下望上好。」眾人即下了雁齒扶梯，仍到第一層，已見正中廓前擺了一個圓桌。此會是賓主四人，名花五人。子雲便要穿衣，經史、田三位止住，只得就便服送了酒，依齒而坐。東首是南湘，子雲命蘭保坐在肩下。西首是春航，肩下是蕙芳。上面是次賢，肩下是漱芳。

　　子雲坐了主位，左右為素蘭、寶珠二人。飲酒的話頭，無非是那幾套，且慢講他。

　　再看那龍舟已到閣前，盤盤旋旋，來來往往，蕩個不了。

　　家人遠遠的放了五千一串的全紅百子，響得不住。大家正看得喝采，忽見闌干外走上四個人，穿著綠油綢短衫，紅油綢褲，赤膊拴腰，紅巾紮額，赤了腳，穿著草鞋，腿上纏緊了藍布，站齊在闌干前，對上叩了一個頭。南湘不解其故，待要問時，只聽龍舟一聲鼓響，那四個人齊齊的倒翻筋斗下水去了。子雲道：「這些蠢奴，他們也要顯些本領。」遂命家人去捉幾對鴨子來，又叫取幾個紅漆葫蘆拋下水去，眾人方曉得是奪標。家人答應，便將一個白鴨先拋下水去，那鴨子下了水，把頭一鑽也翻了一個筋斗，便伸著頭，拍著翅，呷、呷、呷的叫了幾聲。

　　那邊一人便俯在水面，兩腳一蹬，似梭子的穿過來。那鴨子見人來拿他，便扇起雙翅，半沉半浮，走得風快。正走時，忽見水裡探出個頭來，一手把鴨子捉住。子雲道：「好！記著賞他。」又將三隻鴨子，兩個葫蘆同拋下去。這四個人各要討好，都竭盡其藝，或俯或仰，或沉或浮，或側半面，或蹺一腿，游來游去，頑個不了。也有拿著的，也有拿不著的，也有拿到了，重新脫手的，也有拿到半路，被人奪去的，引得席上個個歡笑，各人飲了好幾杯。那些相公們更覺高興，都出了席，靠著闌干看玩藝。

　　子雲叫了進來，再斟了酒。次賢道：「我們今日就以此為令何如？」眾人問道：「怎樣做令？」次賢問那些家人道：「去年園中結那些大葫蘆，想來還有。」家人應道：「有十幾個漆的，其餘是沒有漆的。」次賢便叫把漆的拿來。不多一刻，家人就提了一大串來，解開繩子，放在一張空桌上。次賢又叫拿那副酒籌來。家人又送上一個象牙酒籌。次賢隨手抽出幾枝，便把沒有字的一面朝上，放在桌上，對眾人道：「各人隨手取一根，不准看那一面的字，各人注上各人的號。」大家就依了他。

　　次賢便把葫蘆揭開蓋子，每一個放下一個酒籌，仍舊將蓋子旋緊，命家童拋下水去。」看拿到那一個的，便是那一個喝酒，這是極公道的頑意兒。」眾人道：「極是，但不知籌上寫些什麼。」次賢道：「方才這副籌，是《水滸傳》上的人，各有飲酒的故事，我是隨手數的，不知是那幾個名字。」子雲笑道：「這籌倒也好，喝得爽快。就是內中有幾個大量的，抽著了卻是難為。」眾人道：「這也只好聽天由命了。」只見水中搶了一個出來，家童拿到席邊將手巾擦乾了，開了蓋子，倒出籌來，是蕭次賢的。大家看那一面時，刻著七個大字，下注兩行小字。大字是：「李逵大鬧潯陽江。」注是：「首二坐為宋江、戴宗，末坐邊張順，李逵自飲一大杯，宋、戴陪飲一小杯，即與張順豁十拳。李逵贏拳，張順吃酒；張順贏拳，李逵喝開水。」眾人看了皆笑。次賢先飲了門面杯，南湘、春航陪了一杯。即與子雲猜拳，子雲飲了六杯酒，次賢飲了四杯茶。眾人道：「倒也有趣。」又見拿了一個上來，看籌是南湘的。那面是：「武松醉奪快活林。」下注：無三不過崗，先滿飲三杯。對面為蔣門神，要連勝三拳方過，再打通關一轉。」南湘道：「這一回太多了，三杯我就喝，這通關免了罷。」子雲道：「免是不能免的，況且你是個大量。」蘭保道：「打通關或用半杯，或一杯分作三消罷。」眾人亦皆依了。南湘吃了三杯，即與春航豁起拳來，倒也連勝了三拳，又打了一個通關，共吃了十二杯酒。

　　又見水中拿了兩個出來，第一個揭出來是徐字雲的。那面是：「宋江怒殺閻婆惜。」注：「飲兩杯，並坐者為閻婆惜，宋江先自飲一杯，將一杯勸閻婆惜，婆惜不飲，仍是宋江自飲。

　　「子雲笑道：「座中誰是閻婆惜呢？」眾人笑了。次賢道：「不消說，是並肩坐的這兩個了，且仍是你自飲，用是用不著他們，但勸是要勸的。」子雲帶笑飲了一杯，又將一杯對素蘭道：「香畹你是個好人，你莫要學那閻婆惜，心上只記著張三郎，不瞅不睬的，你且飲這一杯罷。」引得眾人笑起來。素蘭本待要飲，因為眾人一笑，便臉上紅暈了一層，便把嘴向著寶珠一呶，說道：「閻婆惜在那邊，你叫他飲罷。」寶珠也嗤的一笑。子雲又拿一杯對著寶珠道：「如何，你飲不飲？」寶珠接了杯子，對著素蘭道：「你上了當了，你看籌上不飲的是閻婆惜，飲的就不是了。」即將酒飲盡。素蘭一想，倒被寶珠討了便宜。再拿那一根籌看時，是蕙芳的。再看那面，眾人就笑起來，只有田春航強住了笑，臉上卻有些紅。原來這一根籌偏偏是蕙芳，也是捉弄潘三的報應。上寫著：「潘金蓮雪天戲叔。」注：「三杯，並坐左邊的為武松。第一杯要露出了胸，一手搭在武松肩上，叫聲『叔叔，你飲這一杯。』第二杯要自吃半杯，又道：『叔叔，你若有心就吃這半杯兒殘酒。』第三杯要站起來，裝作怒容自飲，合席陪飲三杯。」當下蕙芳就不肯，道：「我們豁了這三杯罷。」子雲道：「這是令上寫明白的，水裡撈出來的，豈可改得？」次賢道：「況且是你親手寫在籌上的，如今怎好翻悔？」南湘道：「你如要改令，方才我們又何必照樣呢？」蕙芳無奈，躊躇了半天，蘭保笑道：「報應之快，如今是真要上那姓潘的當了。」眾人不甚明白，只道是籌上的潘金蓮，卻不曉得蘭保是聽見潘三的事。春航心內明白，只低頭不語。蕙芳聽了一發臉紅，也不理他，只得拿了一杯酒，站起來靠著寶珠道：「叔叔，你吃這杯罷？」寶珠正在吃菜，不提防蕙芳叫他這一聲，便笑得噴了一桌，靠住了子雲，把手巾擦了嘴，還笑個不住。眾人哄然皆笑起來。蕙芳弄得沒法，放下杯子，自己也笑了。次賢道：「媚香，又錯了，你不看注指並坐左鄰為武松，不是右邊的人，怎麼把這杯酒敬起瑤卿來？」蕙芳道：「你到底要我敬那一個呢？他不是與我並坐的嗎？」寶珠道：「我恰好不算並坐。雖然是圓桌，我卻朝北，你是向東，我再料不到你叫我叔叔。」說罷又笑了，蕙芳終是不肯。子雲笑道：「媚香，你難道沒有敬過湘帆的酒麼？快此，快些！你看又撈起兩個來了。你若壞了令，後來怎樣？不過好歹這一次，又沒有三回兩回輪著你的。」次賢道：「快敬罷！」南湘道：「當年金蓮戲叔之時，是要做些媚態方像，不可老老實實的。「你一句，我一言，大家逼著，蕙芳真是無奈，不道尖利人也有吃虧時候。蕙芳只得略靠著春航，擎起了杯道：「叔叔，吃這一杯。」春航也是無奈，只得老著臉飲了。第二杯蕙芳也只得先飲了一口，送到春航口邊，春航不待叫，就飲了。眾人皆說：「這杯不算，重來，令上是要叫明才算的。」春航再三求情，只得算了。到了第三杯，卻甚容易。蕙芳自斟了一杯，立起身來。次賢道：「這杯要作怒容的。」素蘭道：「他心中本有氣。」蕙芳一笑，又忙將花容一整，做出怒態，便一口乾了。子雲看了這光景，心上十分贊賞，便自己飲了三杯，又勸合席也飲三杯。

　　於是再看籌時是蘭保的。那面是：「魯智深醉打山門。」注：「先飲一大杯，首二坐為金剛，每人豁三拳。」蕙芳道：「他就這等便宜，我偏這麼囉嗦。」蘭保照令行了，與南湘、春航各豁了三拳。

　　再看籌是漱芳的，那面是：「金翠蓮酒樓賣唱。要彈琵琶，敬魯達、李忠、史進各一杯。」眾人道：「這還可以，在不即不離之間。況且真是個姓金的，怎麼遇得這般湊巧？」漱芳只得彈起琵琶，敬了南湘、春航、次賢三人。

　　再看葫蘆內籌是田春航。春航急看那一面，想一想，又說聲：「不好！」眾人又復拍手大笑道：「今日就是媚香與湘帆牽纏不清。」蕙芳紅著臉道：「這是你們有心做成的，不然為什麼單是這兩根籌這麼樣呢？」次賢道：「冤枉冤哉！算我有心撿出的，難道你們又有心撿過去嗎？」原來籌上寫的是：「一丈青捉王短虎。」注：「後成夫婦，與並坐的手牽紅巾，飲三個交杯，合席共賀一杯。」春航欲要改令，怎禁得大家不依，只得拿塊帕子與蕙芳遞著，各飲了半杯，第三次惹得合席說了又笑，笑了又說，道：「這個合巹杯，是難得見的，我們各浮一大白。」於是合席又賀了一杯，更把蕙芳臊得了不得，便道：「從此難星也過完了，等我可以取笑人了。」看籌是寶珠的。那面是：「王婆樓上說風情。」看了注，蕙芳笑道：「今番卻有報應了，不料也有人做那好樣兒與人看了。」寶珠的臉已經紅暈了半邊。令是三杯酒：第一杯是敬右鄰為西門慶，也做成挑簾的樣了，將扇子打西門慶一下，敬這一杯。第二杯要西門慶跪地，一手捏著金蓮的鞋尖，敬金蓮這一杯。第三杯，左鄰是王婆，金蓮福了一福，叫聲：「乾娘！飲這一杯。」子雲笑道：「可可如今輪到我了。」春航道：「香塵沾漆是件最美的事，況且蓮鉤在握，就飲十杯何妨？」南湘大笑道：「香塵沾膝還可以，只不要跪在爛泥裡，那時蓮鉤倒摸不著，摸著的是條驢腿。」說得眾人哄然狂笑起來，把個金漱芳笑得閃了腰，直跌到次賢懷裡。王蘭保、陸素蘭笑得走開了。寶珠道：「此又是報應，天理昭彰，一毫不爽的。」大家笑得春航十分難受，又不好認真，只得忍住道：「竹君刻薄，應該罰他一個惡令。」南湘笑道：「我是據實而言，何刻薄之有？」蕙芳道：「你也夠了，不要說嘴，曉得也有失風時候。」次賢笑道：「瑤卿，此令如何？看來是不能改的，只好委屈些罷。倒難為了度香這膝下黃金了。」眾人又復大笑。蕙芳即催寶珠快些敬酒，寶珠是個溫柔性氣的人，被眾人逼不過，只得老著臉，將扇子把子雲輕輕打了一下，敬過這杯酒。子雲笑而受之，眾人說聲：「好！我們也各飲一杯。」子雲道：「酒令嚴於軍令，沒奈何，諸公休笑矮人觀場。」只得斟了一杯酒，屈了一膝，來敬寶珠，寶珠連忙接過飲了。眾人又說聲：「好！」又各飲一杯。寶珠便將這第三杯酒對著蕙芳，福了一福道：「乾娘，請飲這杯。」蕙芳接來飲了，笑道：「好女兒，生受你。」眾人皆贊道：「好個乾娘、乾女兒，我們再賀一杯。」又各飲了。便剩下一根籌，知是素蘭，取來看時是：「梁山泊群雄聚義。」合席各飲三杯。眾人道：「這卻收得有趣，今日這個酒令，真倒像做成的一般。」寶珠道：「只是太便宜了他，又便宜了靜芳，瘦香還彈了一彈琵琶。第一是我與媚香才算不來呢。」

　　蕙芳道：「有人跪了你敬酒，還不好？還要怎樣？」寶珠道：「你要人跪你，方才何不代我行了這個令？」此一回酒已飲到紅日沉西，也就吃了飯。

　　盥漱畢，又飲了一回香茗，南湘道：「還有小赤城的榴花沒有賞鑒，何不就趁著晚霞掩映，看那榴火如焚不好嗎？」子雲即引眾復坐船回過紅橋，到西邊假山前上岸，從神仙洞走出，穿過了杏樓、桃塢兩處，便是小赤城。只見榴花回繞如城，約有一二百株，紅霞閃爍，流火欲燃，間有幾種黃白及瑪瑙等色，相間而開。正是《天臺山賦》上的「赤城霞起而建標」，所以叫做小赤城。

　　天色已晚，南湘、春航要回，小使送上衣帽，各人穿戴，謝了主人並次賢，繞道出園。子雲道：「今日本有一事要煩兩兄。園中各處的對聯尚須添設幾副，今日倒被龍舟耽誤了，遲日再請一遊，並約庾香、劍潭諸君何如？」史、田二人應了，遂上車而去。這邊相公五人，也各陸續散去。這回怡園二次宴客，可惜人少未齊，不曉下卷又敘何人，再俟細細想來。

In the previous chapter, it was mentioned that Pan San was entangled with Huifang, and at a critical moment, someone suddenly shouted and came in. Huifang pretended to be startled and said, “This is terrible! The local officials are checking the night!” Pan San, being a wealthy but timid man, naturally got scared and had to slip away.

Huifang had already anticipated that Pan San would not give up easily today while he was in the kitchen. He had arranged for someone at home to pretend to be the local officials checking the night and had also invited two actual officials. When Pan San started to behave inappropriately, they would come in shouting. Knowing that Pan San was bold in his desires but timid at heart, he indeed fell for the trick and left, allowing Huifang to avoid him once again. Although he had obtained a gold bracelet from him, Huifang was genuinely worried that he might come again the next day. He decided to hide at Chunhang’s place for a few days and see how things would go. Pan San returned home in low spirits, fearful of his wife and unable to behave recklessly in public. Otherwise, even though Huifang was clever, he might have found it hard to handle him. Having caused a scene in vain today, he could only slowly use money to win him back again.

This chapter will talk about a few cultured people doing elegant things. The group of notable scholars gradually dispersed. Since the last gathering at Yiyuan, Ziyu had not been able to meet Qinyan again.

Qinyan’s illness was intermittent, and he did not perform in the garden. Sometimes, he forced himself to visit Yiyuan despite his illness.

Ziyu’s illness was also caused by worries. Sometimes when he went to Yiyuan, Qinyan was not there; other times, when he went to Qinyan’s residence, Qinyan was either entertaining guests or otherwise occupied. Ziyu also found it inconvenient to seek out Sulan, feeling helpless and lamenting the missed connections. Qinyan, unaware of Ziyu’s visits, heard that Ziyu was ill and felt even more sorrowful. Since he had never been to the Mei residence, he couldn’t go there on his own. His admiration for Ziyu’s talent and appearance remained unresolved, leaving him sighing and longing even in his dreams.

The reader might wonder why Qinyan’s master did not facilitate their meeting. Firstly, Ziyu was not a frequent visitor, and Changqing did not know him well, seeing him only as a young scholar with little importance. Secondly, Ziyu had never spent money on Qinyan, as their connection was based on mutual respect and intellectual affinity, not on financial transactions. Changqing, however, valued money over character. This was typical of such performers and remained unchanged in Changqing’s nature.

Ziyu was at home recovering from his illness, not going out. Gaopin was invited by Governor Hu of Hejian to compile records. Liu Wenze, concerned by his mother-in-law, came to take him and his wife, Wu, to the governor’s office in Zhili. With three people missing, only Ziyun, Cixian, Nanxiang, Zhongqing, Chunhang, and Wang Xun remained in occasional contact.

One day, Ziyun and Cixian invited notable scholars to the garden to watch dragon boat races and enjoy pomegranate blossoms. It was the first day of May, coinciding with the birthday of Wang Tongzheng. Although he did not celebrate, some close friends, relatives, and colleagues came to congratulate him, including Madam Yan from the Mei residence and Madam Lu from the Sun residence, making it lively. Wang Xun and Zhongqing could not go to Yiyuan as planned. Ziyun and Cixian, aware of this, also went to pay respects and met Nanxiang and Chunhang there, inviting them back. Zhongqing and Wang Xun promised to join later if the guests left early.

After paying respects, they returned to Yiyuan and went to a courtyard under a cliff. Ziyun invited everyone to take off their formal attire due to the heat. He suggested they ride horses to see the dragon boats and pomegranate blossoms as they were far apart. The servants had prepared horses, and the four rode off. They followed a winding path, surrounded by ancient vines and fragrant plants. The path led along a wall beside a rippling pond, shaded by willows and adorned with flowers and birds. After half a mile, they encountered a tall rock formation, blocking their way.

They dismounted and climbed a flight of stone steps to a small pavilion named “Piaomiao Pavilion.” From there, they saw tall pines and a corner of a red building through the trees. The cool breeze and the serene atmosphere made them feel as if they were in a different world. Chunhang remarked on the beauty, and Nanxiang commented on the resemblance to famous scenic spots. Ziyun explained that it was all designed by Jingyi, who revised the plans multiple times. The pines enhanced the view, making it more enchanting. They admired the elegant setup, feeling that it rivaled famous landscape paintings.

After a rest, they descended and saw a five-room pavilion with exquisite decorations and a pond with a red bridge leading to more pavilions. They saw small painted boats with luxurious decorations. Cixian pointed out that they had reached “Yinqiu Pavilion.” The scene was picturesque, with willow trees and bamboo groves lining the water’s edge.

Ziyun invited them to cross the bridge and enter the pavilion, which was intricately decorated with precious items. A copper pot with bamboo arrows and a plaque with a poetic couplet added to the elegance. Nanxiang recognized the work of Hua Gongzi, praising his refined taste. They discussed his talent and lamented his unfulfilled potential. As they admired the surroundings, they heard the sound of boats approaching. They saw Wang Lanbao skillfully steering a boat, adorned with pomegranate blossoms and decorated with bamboo poles, adding to the lively scene with ducks and birds flying around.

Cixian laughed and said, “This is what they mean by ‘disturbing the ducks and startling the mandarin ducks.’” Everyone found it amusing and then saw several gentlemen emerging from the boats. One boat had Baozhu and Sufang, while the other had Huifang and Sulan, making five in total. The boatmen docked the boats near the railing. Nanxiang remarked, “The lotuses are not in bloom, so the pavilion looks dull. With these gentlemen crossing over, it won’t be lonely. The fairies of the Xiang River and the goddess of the Luo River are playing by the riverbank. I bet Mr. Xiang will reward them with jade pendants.” Everyone laughed, and the performers came up to greet them.

Cixian commented, “Look at Jingfang in his narrow sleeves, so elegant and poised. Zhu Jun’s praise, ‘Graceful as a startled swan, supple as a swimming dragon,’ is truly apt.” Nanxiang added, “Jingfang’s charm, Meixiang’s wit, Yaoqing’s gentleness, Shouxiang’s beauty, and Xiangwan’s grace are like celestial beings turned human. If we consider their talents, it resembles Zhao Feiyan’s dance on the palm and Zhang Jingwan’s song in the tent.” Ziyun invited the guests to board the boat. Nanxiang and others got on. The boat’s bow was carved with two entwined mandarin ducks, made of pear wood, with short red railings on the sides and long glass windows inside. The canopy was covered with a large green fabric with floral patterns, with white silk painted with flowers hanging on both sides. The boat had two cabins, with fine white rugs on the floor and long windows at the back. The middle section had a couch, with small rattan chairs on both sides and a few tea tables in between. A round table could seat five or six people. A smaller boat followed for the servants. By this time, Wang Lanbao had already changed into clean clothes and was sitting quietly. Baozhu asked Nanxiang, “Did you visit Minister Wang’s house this morning?” Before Nanxiang could reply, Ziyun said, “I invited them from Wang’s residence.”

The group chatted as they admired the scenery in the garden, passing by various pavilions and rock formations, old trees, and gnarled branches. They saw the long corridor in the northwest leading to Peach Grove, followed by Apricot Village. To the north, through the bamboo forest, they saw Pear Yard, followed by the fragrant Peony Garden. In the northeast were delicate mountains, with a thousand trees shading the area and plum fruits hanging heavily, obscuring the view of Plum Cliff. Across the river were more pavilions and courtyards hidden among trees and rocks. Chunhang asked Nanxiang, “How many places have you visited in this garden?” Nanxiang replied, “I’ve been here many times, but I’ve only toured about seven or eight places. Whenever we drink, it takes the whole day, leaving no time for exploring.” Baozhu said, “Shouxiang and I have seen it all.” Huifang added, “I haven’t been to Osmanthus Ridge, Chrysanthemum Path, or Orchid Lane, but I’ve seen the rest.”

Sulan said, “Osmanthus Ridge is in front of the mountain, Orchid Lane and Chrysanthemum Path are behind the mountain. Across the stream is a large open space with a village, which is Chrysanthemum Path. Orchid Lane is halfway up the mountain, with winding corridors and paths, the best place for playing. Beyond Chrysanthemum Path is a rice farm with water wheels and fishing nets, resembling a village, complete with crane enclosures and deer pens nearby.”

As they chatted, the boat sailed for over half a mile, reaching a wide open area of the pond. The Yinqiu Pavilion stood in the water, surrounded by the pond. It had three stories; the first had twelve rooms in a hexagonal layout, each with glass windows and intricate designs, divided into twelve sections, each uniquely shaped. The furnishings inside were too numerous to describe. They toured the first floor for a while. Ziyun said, “Guests must be hungry; it’s almost noon. Let’s sit down.” Four boys brought golden lacquer trays with bowls of almond pudding for everyone. Chunhang suggested, “Let’s visit the other two floors before we sit down.” They climbed to the second floor, which had a four-sided design with a balcony, and the interior was divided into eight sections with elegant decorations. In the northeast corner, they saw a dragon boat decorated with colorful paintings, flags, and ornaments. Chunhang, who had seen similar boats in the south, commented on its splendid design, rivaling the best in Changzhou.

They climbed to the third floor, which had a three-sided design with balconies. The windows and doors were made of fragrant nanmu wood, giving it a rustic and elegant feel. The higher elevation offered a refreshing breeze and a panoramic view of Yiyuan, except for the shaded areas. The scenery resembled a natural painting, with overlapping pavilions, lush flowers and trees, clear springs, and winding streams. The beauty of the garden was comparable to famous paintings and man-made landscapes.

As they admired the view, they heard the melodious sound of drums and flutes from the dragon boat below. The boat, adorned with a swing at the tail, had children playing on it. Cixian suggested they go down to see it up close. They descended the ladder to the first floor, where a round table was set in the central hall. The four hosts and five performers sat around, with Ziyun at the head. They served wine and sat according to rank, with Nanxiang and Ziyun at the east, Chunhang and Huifang at the west, and Cixian and Sufang at the top. Ziyun sat in the host’s seat, flanked by Sulan and Baozhu.

As they drank and chatted, the dragon boat slowly approached the pavilion, moving gracefully on the water. Servants set off strings of firecrackers, adding to the lively atmosphere. Suddenly, four men in green oilcloth jackets, red trousers, and red headbands, barefoot and wearing straw sandals, stood before the railing and bowed. Nanxiang, puzzled, was about to ask when the dragon boat sounded a drumbeat, and the four men somersaulted into the water. Ziyun said, “These silly servants want to show off their skills.” He then ordered servants to fetch some ducks and red lacquer gourds for a game. The servants threw a white duck into the water, which dived and resurfaced, flapping its wings and quacking loudly.

One person leaned over the water and kicked his feet, shooting through the water like a shuttle. Seeing someone coming to catch it, the duck flapped its wings, half-submerging and floating, moving swiftly. As it swam, a head suddenly emerged from the water, and a hand grabbed the duck. Ziyun said, “Good! Remember to reward him.” Then he threw three more ducks and two gourds into the water. The four men, eager to impress, used all their skills—diving, floating, flipping sideways, or kicking one leg—swimming back and forth, putting on quite a show. Some caught the ducks, some didn’t, some caught them only to lose them again, and some had their catch snatched away mid-swim, causing everyone at the table to laugh and drink several cups of wine. The actors were even more delighted, leaving their seats to lean against the railing and watch the spectacle.

Ziyun called everyone back in to pour more wine. Cixian suggested, “How about we make this the game for today?” The others asked, “What’s the game?” Cixian asked the servants, “Those large gourds that grew in the garden last year, are there any left?” The servant replied, “We have about ten lacquered ones; the rest are unvarnished.” Cixian ordered the lacquered ones to be brought. Soon, a servant came with a large string of gourds, untied the string, and placed them on an empty table. Cixian also called for the wine tokens. The servant brought an ivory set of wine tokens. Cixian randomly drew a few and placed them face down on the table, saying to the group, “Everyone pick one without looking at the other side. Mark your own token.” They all complied.

Cixian then opened the gourds, placing one token inside each, and sealed them tightly, instructing the servant to throw them into the water. “Whoever retrieves one will have to drink. It’s a fair game.” Everyone agreed, curious about the inscriptions on the tokens. Cixian explained, “These tokens feature characters from the ‘Water Margin,’ each with a drinking story. I don’t know which names are on them.” Ziyun laughed, “This sounds fun. But some of these characters are known for their heavy drinking, so it might be challenging.” The others agreed, “We’ll just have to see what happens.”

One gourd was retrieved, and the servant wiped it dry and opened it. The token belonged to Xiao Cixian. Everyone saw the inscription, which read, “Li Kui causes havoc at Xunyang River.” The note said, “The first two seats belong to Song Jiang and Dai Zong, the last seat to Zhang Shun. Li Kui drinks a big cup, Song and Dai drink small cups, and Zhang Shun gets ten punches. If Li Kui wins, Zhang Shun drinks; if Zhang Shun wins, Li Kui drinks water.” Everyone laughed. Cixian drank his cup first, with Nanxiang and Chunhang accompanying with their cups. Then he and Ziyun played a drinking game, resulting in Ziyun drinking six cups of wine and Cixian drinking four cups of tea. The group found it amusing.

Another gourd was brought up, and the token belonged to Nanxiang. The inscription read, “Wu Song gets drunk and takes over Happy Forest.” The note said, “Drink three cups first. Then, facing Jiang Menshen, win three consecutive rounds to pass.” Nanxiang said, “That’s too much. I’ll drink the three cups but skip the rounds.” Ziyun objected, “No skipping, especially since you’re a hearty drinker.” Lanbao suggested, “For the rounds, maybe half a cup each time?” Everyone agreed. Nanxiang drank three cups and then won three rounds against Chunhang, ending up drinking twelve cups in total.

Two more gourds were retrieved, and the first token was Ziyun’s. The inscription read, “Song Jiang kills Yan Poxi.” The note said, “Drink two cups. The companion, Yan Poxi, is to drink one. If she refuses, Song Jiang drinks both.” Ziyun joked, “Who is Yan Poxi here?” Everyone laughed. Cixian remarked, “It’s your neighbors; you must drink and persuade them.” Ziyun laughed, drank one cup, and handed the other to Sulan, saying, “Xiangwan, don’t be like Yan Poxi, only caring about Zhang Sanlang. Drink this cup.” This made everyone laugh. Sulan, initially willing to drink, blushed and nodded towards Baozhu, saying, “Yan Poxi is over there; ask her to drink.” Baozhu laughed and took the cup, drinking it while teasing Sulan.

The next token belonged to Huifang. The inscription caused everyone to laugh, except Tian Chunhang, who forced a smile with a slightly red face. The token read, “Pan Jinlian plays with her uncle in the snow.” The note said, “Three cups. The left-hand companion is Wu Song. The first cup must be offered with exposed chest and a hand on Wu Song’s shoulder, saying, ‘Uncle, drink this cup.’ The second cup must be half-drunk, then say, ‘Uncle, if you care, drink the rest.’ The third cup must be drunk standing up, acting angry, with everyone accompanying with three cups.” Huifang refused, “Let’s skip these three cups.” Ziyun insisted, “The rules are clear. It was your idea.” Cixian added, “You wrote these rules yourself; no backing out now.” Nanxiang remarked, “If we change the rules now, what’s the point?”

Huifang, reluctant, hesitated for a long time. Lanbao laughed, “You see, karma is quick. Now it’s your turn to play Pan.” The group, unaware of the story about Pan San, thought it was just the token’s Pan Jinlian. Chunhang, understanding, remained silent. Huifang, blushing even more, had no choice but to take a cup and lean towards Baozhu, saying, “Uncle, drink this cup.” Baozhu, caught off guard while eating, laughed, spraying food everywhere, and leaned on Ziyun, wiping his mouth with a towel. Everyone roared with laughter. Huifang, embarrassed, put the cup down and laughed as well. Cixian remarked, “Meixiang, you got it wrong. The note says the left-hand companion is Wu Song, not the right-hand one. Why offer the cup to Yaoqing?” Huifang, flustered, asked, “Who should I offer it to then? He’s sitting next to me.” Baozhu said, “I’m not exactly beside you. Even though it’s a round table, I’m facing north, and you’re facing east. I never expected you to call me uncle.” Everyone laughed again, but Huifang still refused. Ziyun smiled, “Meixiang, haven’t you ever offered Xiangfan a drink? Do it quickly! Look, they’ve brought up two more tokens. If you break the rule now, what about later? Just do it this once, it won’t come around again.” Cixian urged, “Quick, offer the drink!” Nanxiang added, “When Pan Jinlian played with her uncle, she had to show some charm, not be so serious.”

Everyone chimed in, pressuring Huifang. She had no choice but to lean towards Chunhang, raising her cup, and said, “Uncle, drink this cup.” Chunhang, reluctantly, drank it. For the second cup, Huifang drank half and offered the rest to Chunhang, who drank it without waiting for her to call. The group said, “That doesn’t count, you need to call him.” Chunhang pleaded, but they insisted. For the third cup, Huifang poured and stood up. Cixian said, “This one needs to show anger.” Sulan remarked, “She already has some anger.” Huifang laughed, composed herself, and acted angry, downing the cup in one go. Ziyun, impressed, drank three cups himself and encouraged the group to drink three cups as well.

Next, they looked at the token, and it was Lanbao’s. On it was written: “Lu Zhishen drunkenly beats the monastery gate.” The note said: “Drink a large cup first, then the first two seats, being the Arhats, each compete in three rounds of finger-guessing.” Huifang complained, “He gets it easy while mine was so troublesome.” Lanbao followed the instructions, competing in three rounds each with Nanxiang and Chunhang.

The next token was Sufang’s. On it was written: “Jin Cuilian sings in the tavern.” The note said: “Play the pipa and offer a cup each to Lu Da, Li Zhong, and Shi Jin.” Everyone commented, “That’s reasonable, not too demanding. And how coincidental that it involves someone named Jin.” Sufang played the pipa and offered cups to Nanxiang, Chunhang, and Cixian.

Then, they checked the gourd containing Tian Chunhang’s token. Chunhang quickly glanced at it and exclaimed, “Oh no!” The others laughed and said, “Today, it seems Meixiang and Xiangfan are entangled.” Huifang, blushing, said, “This is deliberately done; why are these two tokens the only ones like this?” Cixian responded, “Unfair accusation! If I had picked them on purpose, how could you have gotten them?” The token read: “Yizhangqing captures Wang Shuanghu.” The note said: “Later becoming husband and wife, hold a red scarf together with the neighbor, drink three cups cross-handed, and everyone else toasts one cup.” Chunhang wanted to change the rule but couldn’t resist the group’s insistence. He reluctantly handed a handkerchief to Huifang, and they each drank half a cup, causing much laughter and jokes. The third time, the whole table toasted, causing Huifang great embarrassment. She remarked, “My unlucky streak is finally over. Now, I can tease others.” The next token belonged to Baozhu, and it read: “Madam Wang speaks flirtatiously upstairs.” The note specified three cups: the first offered to the right-hand neighbor as Ximen Qing, mimicking a curtain-lifting gesture with a fan; the second to be offered to Ximen Qing while kneeling, holding Jinlian’s shoe tip; the third to the left-hand neighbor as Madam Wang, with a bow and greeting “Dry Mother, drink this cup.”

Ziyun laughed, “Now it’s my turn.” Chunhang joked, “It’s delightful to have incense dust on the knees. Ten cups would be fine.” Nanxiang laughed, “As long as you don’t kneel in the mud and grab a donkey’s leg instead of the lotus hook.” This caused an uproar of laughter, with Jin Sufang laughing so hard she fell into Cixian’s arms, and Wang Lanbao and Lu Sulan walked away laughing. Baozhu remarked, “This is retribution; the heavens are just.” Chunhang felt awkward but could only endure it. He jokingly said, “Zhujun, you deserve a penalty for being so mean.” Nanxiang laughed, “I was just stating the truth, not being mean.” Huifang said, “Enough talking, you know everyone has their moments.” Cixian laughed, “Yaoqing, this rule can’t be changed, so you’ll have to endure it. Poor Duxiang.” This caused another round of laughter.

Huifang urged Baozhu to quickly offer the drink. Baozhu, a gentle person, reluctantly used the fan to lightly tap Ziyun, offering the drink. Ziyun accepted it with a smile, and everyone cheered and drank. Ziyun said, “Wine rules are stricter than military rules, so no complaints. Gentlemen, don’t laugh at me.” He then poured a cup of wine, knelt on one knee, and offered it to Baozhu, who hurriedly accepted and drank. Everyone cheered again and drank. Baozhu offered the third cup to Huifang, bowing and saying, “Dry Mother, please drink this cup.” Huifang accepted it with a smile, saying, “Good daughter, thank you.” Everyone praised, “What a good mother and daughter pair! Let’s toast again.” They all drank another cup.

Finally, the last token was Sulan’s. It read: “The heroes gather at Liangshan Marsh.” The note said: “Everyone drinks three cups.” The group commented, “That’s a fitting end, and today’s drinking game seems perfectly arranged.” Baozhu remarked, “It’s too easy for him, and for Jingfang, while Shouxiang had to play the pipa. Only Meixiang and I had it tough.”

Huifang responded, “Someone knelt to offer you a drink, isn’t that good enough?” Baozhu retorted, “If you wanted someone to kneel, why didn’t you take my place?” By this time, the sun was setting, and they ate dinner.

After washing up, they drank fragrant tea. Nanxiang suggested, “We haven’t admired the pomegranate flowers at Little Chicheng. Why not go now, with the evening glow illuminating them?” Ziyun led the group back on the boat, crossing the red bridge to disembark at the western rockery. They walked through the Immortal Cave, passing through Apricot Tower and Peach Grove to reach Little Chicheng. There, they saw a hundred or more pomegranate trees blooming like a fiery city, with red hues flickering and seemingly ablaze, interspersed with yellow, white, and agate-colored flowers. It was like the scene described in “The Rhapsody of Mount Tiantai,” thus named Little Chicheng.

As night fell, Nanxiang and Chunhang prepared to leave. Servants brought their coats and hats, and they thanked the hosts and Cixian before leaving the garden. Ziyun mentioned, “I had something to ask you two. The garden needs more couplets in various spots, but we were delayed by the dragon boat today. Let’s arrange another visit soon and invite Yuxiang and Jiantan as well.” Both Shi and Tian agreed and left by carriage. The five performers also gradually dispersed. This second banquet at Yiyuan, though not fully attended, leaves us wondering who will be featured in the next chapter. Let’s wait and see.
